"""Custom CUDA top-k over the last dim.

Hybrid strategy with preallocated buffers in the Model:
  * k == 1: warp-reduction argmax.
  * batch == 1: single CUB DeviceRadixSort over the row, then copy top-k.
  * batch > 1: CUB BlockRadixSort per 1024-element chunk, then merge per-chunk
    top-k lists in shared memory.
"""
import torch
import torch.nn as nn
from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline


CPP_SOURCE = r'''
#include <torch/extension.h>
#include <vector>

void topk_argmax_forward(torch::Tensor input, int64_t k,
                         torch::Tensor values, torch::Tensor indices,
                         torch::Tensor tmp_vals, torch::Tensor tmp_idx);

void topk_single_row_forward(torch::Tensor input, int64_t k,
                             torch::Tensor values, torch::Tensor indices,
                             torch::Tensor sorted_vals, torch::Tensor sorted_idx,
                             torch::Tensor idx_in, torch::Tensor temp_storage);

void topk_batched_forward(torch::Tensor input, int64_t k,
                          torch::Tensor values, torch::Tensor indices,
                          torch::Tensor tmp_vals, torch::Tensor tmp_idx);
'''

CUDA_SOURCE = r'''
#include <torch/extension.h>
#include <cuda_runtime.h>
#include <cfloat>
#include <cstdint>
#include <vector>
#include <cub/block/block_radix_sort.cuh>
#include <cub/device/device_radix_sort.cuh>

constexpr int BLOCK_THREADS = 256;
constexpr int CHUNK_SIZE = 1024;
constexpr int ITEMS_PER_THREAD = CHUNK_SIZE / BLOCK_THREADS;   // 4
constexpr int K_MAX = 64;
constexpr int ARGMAX_CHUNK = 4096;

// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
// Bitonic sort for small runtime-sized arrays of float+int64.
// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
__device__ __forceinline__ void bitonic_sort_descending_runtime(float* __restrict__ vals,
                                                                 int64_t* __restrict__ idx,
                                                                 int N) {
    for (int kk = 2; kk <= N; kk <<= 1) {
        for (int j = kk >> 1; j > 0; j >>= 1) {
            for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < N; i += blockDim.x) {
                if ((i & j) == 0) {
                    int ixj = i ^ j;
                    bool up = (i & kk) != 0;
                    float vi = vals[i];
                    float vj = vals[ixj];
                    bool swap = up ? (vi > vj) : (vi < vj);
                    if (swap) {
                        vals[i] = vj;
                        vals[ixj] = vi;
                        int64_t ii = idx[i];
                        int64_t ij = idx[ixj];
                        idx[i] = ij;
                        idx[ixj] = ii;
                    }
                }
            }
            __syncthreads();
        }
    }
}

// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
// k == 1: argmax per chunk, then merge per row.
// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
__global__ void argmax_chunk_kernel(const float* __restrict__ input,
                                    int batch, int n,
                                    float* __restrict__ out_vals,
                                    int64_t* __restrict__ out_idx,
                                    int blocks_per_row) {
    int row = blockIdx.x;
    int chunk = blockIdx.y;
    int tid = threadIdx.x;
    if (row >= batch) return;

    int chunk_start = chunk * ARGMAX_CHUNK;
    int chunk_end = min(chunk_start + ARGMAX_CHUNK, n);
    const float* row_ptr = input + row * n;

    float local_max = -FLT_MAX;
    int64_t local_idx = 0;
    for (int i = chunk_start + tid; i < chunk_end; i += blockDim.x) {
        float v = row_ptr[i];
        if (v > local_max) {
            local_max = v;
            local_idx = i;
        }
    }

    #pragma unroll
    for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) {
        float other_val = __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, local_max, offset);
        int64_t other_idx = __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, local_idx, offset);
        if (other_val > local_max) {
            local_max = other_val;
            local_idx = other_idx;
        }
    }

    __shared__ float warp_max[BLOCK_THREADS / 32];
    __shared__ int64_t warp_idx[BLOCK_THREADS / 32];
    int lane = tid & 31;
    int warp_id = tid >> 5;
    if (lane == 0) {
        warp_max[warp_id] = local_max;
        warp_idx[warp_id] = local_idx;
    }
    __syncthreads();

    if (tid < (BLOCK_THREADS / 32)) {
        local_max = warp_max[tid];
        local_idx = warp_idx[tid];
    } else {
        local_max = -FLT_MAX;
        local_idx = 0;
    }
    __syncthreads();

    #pragma unroll
    for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) {
        float other_val = __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, local_max, offset);
        int64_t other_idx = __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, local_idx, offset);
        if (other_val > local_max) {
            local_max = other_val;
            local_idx = other_idx;
        }
    }

    if (tid == 0) {
        int out_offset = row * blocks_per_row + chunk;
        out_vals[out_offset] = local_max;
        out_idx[out_offset] = local_idx;
    }
}

__global__ void argmax_merge_kernel(const float* __restrict__ in_vals,
                                    const int64_t* __restrict__ in_idx,
                                    int batch, int blocks_per_row,
                                    float* __restrict__ out_vals,
                                    int64_t* __restrict__ out_idx) {
    int row = blockIdx.x;
    int tid = threadIdx.x;
    if (row >= batch) return;

    float local_max = -FLT_MAX;
    int64_t local_idx = 0;
    int in_offset = row * blocks_per_row;
    for (int i = tid; i < blocks_per_row; i += blockDim.x) {
        float v = in_vals[in_offset + i];
        if (v > local_max) {
            local_max = v;
            local_idx = in_idx[in_offset + i];
        }
    }

    #pragma unroll
    for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) {
        float other_val = __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, local_max, offset);
        int64_t other_idx = __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, local_idx, offset);
        if (other_val > local_max) {
            local_max = other_val;
            local_idx = other_idx;
        }
    }

    __shared__ float warp_max[BLOCK_THREADS / 32];
    __shared__ int64_t warp_idx[BLOCK_THREADS / 32];
    int lane = tid & 31;
    int warp_id = tid >> 5;
    if (lane == 0) {
        warp_max[warp_id] = local_max;
        warp_idx[warp_id] = local_idx;
    }
    __syncthreads();

    if (tid < (BLOCK_THREADS / 32)) {
        local_max = warp_max[tid];
        local_idx = warp_idx[tid];
    } else {
        local_max = -FLT_MAX;
        local_idx = 0;
    }
    __syncthreads();

    #pragma unroll
    for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) {
        float other_val = __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, local_max, offset);
        int64_t other_idx = __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, local_idx, offset);
        if (other_val > local_max) {
            local_max = other_val;
            local_idx = other_idx;
        }
    }

    if (tid == 0) {
        out_vals[row] = local_max;
        out_idx[row] = local_idx;
    }
}

// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
// Level 1 chunk sort: CUB BlockRadixSort for batch > 1.
// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
__global__ void topk_chunk_kernel(const float* __restrict__ input,
                                  int batch, int n, int k,
                                  float* __restrict__ out_vals,
                                  int64_t* __restrict__ out_idx,
                                  int blocks_per_row) {
    using BlockRadixSort = cub::BlockRadixSort<float, BLOCK_THREADS, ITEMS_PER_THREAD, int64_t>;
    __shared__ typename BlockRadixSort::TempStorage temp_storage;

    int row = blockIdx.x;
    int chunk = blockIdx.y;
    int tid = threadIdx.x;
    if (row >= batch) return;

    int chunk_start = chunk * CHUNK_SIZE;
    int chunk_end = min(chunk_start + CHUNK_SIZE, n);
    const float* row_ptr = input + row * n;

    float thread_keys[ITEMS_PER_THREAD];
    int64_t thread_values[ITEMS_PER_THREAD];

    #pragma unroll
    for (int i = 0; i < ITEMS_PER_THREAD; ++i) {
        int pos = chunk_start + tid + i * BLOCK_THREADS;
        if (pos < chunk_end) {
            thread_keys[i] = row_ptr[pos];
            thread_values[i] = pos;
        } else {
            thread_keys[i] = -FLT_MAX;
            thread_values[i] = 0;
        }
    }

    BlockRadixSort(temp_storage).SortDescendingBlockedToStriped(thread_keys, thread_values);

    if (tid < k) {
        int out_offset = row * blocks_per_row * k + chunk * k;
        out_vals[out_offset + tid] = thread_keys[0];
        out_idx[out_offset + tid] = thread_values[0];
    }
}

// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
// Level 2 merge per-chunk top-k lists into the final top-k.
// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
__global__ void topk_merge_kernel(const float* __restrict__ in_vals,
                                  const int64_t* __restrict__ in_idx,
                                  int batch, int blocks_per_row, int k,
                                  float* __restrict__ out_vals,
                                  int64_t* __restrict__ out_idx) {
    extern __shared__ char smem[];
    int row = blockIdx.x;
    int tid = threadIdx.x;
    if (row >= batch) return;

    int total = blocks_per_row * k;
    int N = 1;
    while (N < total) N <<= 1;

    float* svals = reinterpret_cast<float*>(smem);
    int64_t* sidx = reinterpret_cast<int64_t*>(smem + N * sizeof(float));

    int in_offset = row * blocks_per_row * k;
    for (int i = tid; i < N; i += blockDim.x) {
        if (i < total) {
            svals[i] = in_vals[in_offset + i];
            sidx[i] = in_idx[in_offset + i];
        } else {
            svals[i] = -FLT_MAX;
            sidx[i] = 0;
        }
    }
    __syncthreads();

    bitonic_sort_descending_runtime(svals, sidx, N);

    for (int i = tid; i < k; i += blockDim.x) {
        out_vals[row * k + i] = svals[i];
        out_idx[row * k + i] = sidx[i];
    }
}

// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
// Copy first k elements after a full-row sort (batch == 1 path).
// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
__global__ void copy_topk_kernel(const float* __restrict__ sorted_vals,
                                 const int64_t* __restrict__ sorted_idx,
                                 int n, int k,
                                 float* __restrict__ out_vals,
                                 int64_t* __restrict__ out_idx) {
    int tid = threadIdx.x;
    for (int i = tid; i < k; i += blockDim.x) {
        out_vals[i] = sorted_vals[i];
        out_idx[i] = sorted_idx[i];
    }
}

// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
// Exported Python-callable entry points (buffers are preallocated by Model).
// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
void topk_argmax_forward(torch::Tensor input, int64_t k,
                         torch::Tensor values, torch::Tensor indices,
                         torch::Tensor tmp_vals, torch::Tensor tmp_idx) {
    int batch = input.size(0);
    int n = input.size(1);
    int blocks_per_row = (n + ARGMAX_CHUNK - 1) / ARGMAX_CHUNK;

    if (blocks_per_row == 1) {
        dim3 grid(batch, 1);
        argmax_chunk_kernel<<<grid, BLOCK_THREADS>>>(
            input.data_ptr<float>(), batch, n,
            values.data_ptr<float>(), indices.data_ptr<int64_t>(), 1);
    } else {
        dim3 grid1(batch, blocks_per_row);
        argmax_chunk_kernel<<<grid1, BLOCK_THREADS>>>(
            input.data_ptr<float>(), batch, n,
            tmp_vals.data_ptr<float>(), tmp_idx.data_ptr<int64_t>(), blocks_per_row);

        argmax_merge_kernel<<<batch, BLOCK_THREADS>>>(
            tmp_vals.data_ptr<float>(), tmp_idx.data_ptr<int64_t>(),
            batch, blocks_per_row,
            values.data_ptr<float>(), indices.data_ptr<int64_t>());
    }
}

void topk_single_row_forward(torch::Tensor input, int64_t k,
                             torch::Tensor values, torch::Tensor indices,
                             torch::Tensor sorted_vals, torch::Tensor sorted_idx,
                             torch::Tensor idx_in, torch::Tensor temp_storage) {
    int n = input.size(1);
    int kk = static_cast<int>(k);

    size_t temp_bytes = temp_storage.numel();
    cub::DeviceRadixSort::SortPairsDescending(
        temp_storage.data_ptr<uint8_t>(), temp_bytes,
        input.data_ptr<float>(), sorted_vals.data_ptr<float>(),
        idx_in.data_ptr<int64_t>(), sorted_idx.data_ptr<int64_t>(),
        n);

    copy_topk_kernel<<<1, BLOCK_THREADS>>>(
        sorted_vals.data_ptr<float>(), sorted_idx.data_ptr<int64_t>(),
        n, kk,
        values.data_ptr<float>(), indices.data_ptr<int64_t>());
}

void topk_batched_forward(torch::Tensor input, int64_t k,
                          torch::Tensor values, torch::Tensor indices,
                          torch::Tensor tmp_vals, torch::Tensor tmp_idx) {
    int batch = input.size(0);
    int n = input.size(1);
    int kk = static_cast<int>(k);
    int blocks_per_row = (n + CHUNK_SIZE - 1) / CHUNK_SIZE;

    dim3 grid1(batch, blocks_per_row);
    topk_chunk_kernel<<<grid1, BLOCK_THREADS>>>(
        input.data_ptr<float>(), batch, n, kk,
        tmp_vals.data_ptr<float>(), tmp_idx.data_ptr<int64_t>(), blocks_per_row);

    int total = blocks_per_row * kk;
    int merge_N = 1;
    while (merge_N < total) merge_N <<= 1;
    size_t merge_smem = static_cast<size_t>(merge_N) * (sizeof(float) + sizeof(int64_t));

    cudaFuncSetAttribute(topk_merge_kernel,
                         cudaFuncAttributeMaxDynamicSharedMemorySize,
                         static_cast<int>(merge_smem));

    topk_merge_kernel<<<batch, BLOCK_THREADS, merge_smem>>>(
        tmp_vals.data_ptr<float>(), tmp_idx.data_ptr<int64_t>(),
        batch, blocks_per_row, kk,
        values.data_ptr<float>(), indices.data_ptr<int64_t>());
}

// Fallback convenience function (not used by Model, but kept for parity).
std::vector<torch::Tensor> topk_forward(torch::Tensor input, int64_t k) {
    int batch = input.size(0);
    int n = input.size(1);
    auto values = torch::empty({batch, static_cast<int64_t>(k)}, input.options());
    auto indices = torch::empty({batch, static_cast<int64_t>(k)},
                                torch::dtype(torch::kInt64).device(input.device()));

    if (k == 1) {
        int blocks_per_row = (n + ARGMAX_CHUNK - 1) / ARGMAX_CHUNK;
        auto tmp_vals = blocks_per_row > 1
                            ? torch::empty({batch, blocks_per_row}, input.options())
                            : torch::Tensor();
        auto tmp_idx = blocks_per_row > 1
                            ? torch::empty({batch, blocks_per_row},
                                           torch::dtype(torch::kInt64).device(input.device()))
                            : torch::Tensor();
        topk_argmax_forward(input, k, values, indices, tmp_vals, tmp_idx);
    } else if (batch == 1) {
        auto sorted_vals = torch::empty_like(input);
        auto sorted_idx = torch::empty({batch, n}, torch::dtype(torch::kInt64).device(input.device()));
        auto idx_in = torch::arange(n, torch::dtype(torch::kInt64).device(input.device()))
                          .unsqueeze(0)
                          .expand({batch, n})
                          .contiguous();

        size_t temp_bytes = 0;
        cub::DeviceRadixSort::SortPairsDescending(
            nullptr, temp_bytes,
            input.data_ptr<float>(), sorted_vals.data_ptr<float>(),
            idx_in.data_ptr<int64_t>(), sorted_idx.data_ptr<int64_t>(),
            n);
        auto temp_storage = torch::empty({static_cast<int64_t>(temp_bytes)},
                                         torch::dtype(torch::kUInt8).device(input.device()));
        topk_single_row_forward(input, k, values, indices,
                                sorted_vals, sorted_idx, idx_in, temp_storage);
    } else {
        int blocks_per_row = (n + CHUNK_SIZE - 1) / CHUNK_SIZE;
        auto tmp_vals = torch::empty({batch, blocks_per_row, k}, input.options());
        auto tmp_idx = torch::empty({batch, blocks_per_row, k},
                                    torch::dtype(torch::kInt64).device(input.device()));
        topk_batched_forward(input, k, values, indices, tmp_vals, tmp_idx);
    }

    return {values, indices};
}
'''


def _load_kernel():
    return load_inline(
        name="topk_prealloc_sm120",
        cpp_sources=CPP_SOURCE,
        cuda_sources=CUDA_SOURCE,
        functions=[
            "topk_forward",
            "topk_argmax_forward",
            "topk_single_row_forward",
            "topk_batched_forward",
        ],
        extra_cuda_cflags=[
            "-O3",
            "--use_fast_math",
            "-gencode", "arch=compute_120,code=sm_120",
        ],
        verbose=False,
    )


_topk_cuda = _load_kernel()


class Model(nn.Module):
    """Top-k over the last dim of a 2D tensor.

    Input:
        x: (batch, n) fp32
    Output:
        values:  (batch, k) fp32, sorted descending
        indices: (batch, k) int64, into the last dim of x
    """

    def __init__(self, batch: int, n: int, k: int):
        super().__init__()
        self.batch, self.n, self.k = batch, n, k
        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1))

        device = torch.device("cuda:0")

        self.values = torch.empty(batch, k, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
        self.indices = torch.empty(batch, k, dtype=torch.int64, device=device)

        if k == 1:
            blocks_per_row = (n + 4096 - 1) // 4096
            if blocks_per_row > 1:
                self.tmp_vals = torch.empty(batch, blocks_per_row, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
                self.tmp_idx = torch.empty(batch, blocks_per_row, dtype=torch.int64, device=device)
            else:
                self.tmp_vals = torch.empty(0, device=device)
                self.tmp_idx = torch.empty(0, device=device)
            self.fn = _topk_cuda.topk_argmax_forward
        elif batch == 1:
            self.sorted_vals = torch.empty_like(torch.empty(batch, n, dtype=torch.float32, device=device))
            self.sorted_idx = torch.empty(batch, n, dtype=torch.int64, device=device)
            self.idx_in = torch.arange(n, dtype=torch.int64, device=device).unsqueeze(0).expand(batch, n).contiguous()

            # Compute CUB temp storage size once.
            tmp = torch.empty(batch, n, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
            sorted_vals = torch.empty_like(tmp)
            sorted_idx = torch.empty(batch, n, dtype=torch.int64, device=device)
            idx_in = self.idx_in.clone()
            temp_bytes = torch.utils.cpp_extension.load_inline(
                name="temp_size_query",
                cpp_sources="",
                cuda_sources=r'''
#include <torch/extension.h>
#include <cub/device/device_radix_sort.cuh>
int64_t temp_size(torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor idx_in) {
    size_t temp_bytes = 0;
    cub::DeviceRadixSort::SortPairsDescending(
        nullptr, temp_bytes,
        input.data_ptr<float>(), static_cast<float*>(nullptr),
        idx_in.data_ptr<int64_t>(), static_cast<int64_t*>(nullptr),
        input.size(1));
    return static_cast<int64_t>(temp_bytes);
}
PYBIND11_MODULE(TORCH_EXTENSION_NAME, m) { m.def("temp_size", &temp_size); }
''',
                functions=["temp_size"],
                extra_cuda_cflags=["-O3", "-gencode", "arch=compute_120,code=sm_120"],
                verbose=False,
            ).temp_size(tmp, idx_in)

            self.temp_storage = torch.empty(temp_bytes, dtype=torch.uint8, device=device)
            self.fn = _topk_cuda.topk_single_row_forward
        else:
            blocks_per_row = (n + 1024 - 1) // 1024
            self.tmp_vals = torch.empty(batch, blocks_per_row, k, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
            self.tmp_idx = torch.empty(batch, blocks_per_row, k, dtype=torch.int64, device=device)
            self.fn = _topk_cuda.topk_batched_forward

    def forward(self, x: torch.Tensor):
        if self.k == 1:
            self.fn(x, self.k, self.values, self.indices, self.tmp_vals, self.tmp_idx)
        elif self.batch == 1:
            self.fn(x, self.k, self.values, self.indices,
                    self.sorted_vals, self.sorted_idx, self.idx_in, self.temp_storage)
        else:
            self.fn(x, self.k, self.values, self.indices, self.tmp_vals, self.tmp_idx)
        return self.values, self.indices


def get_inputs():
    x = torch.randn(batch, n, dtype=torch.float32)
    return [x]


def get_init_inputs():
    return [batch, n, k]

17	    """Top-k over the last dim of a 2D tensor.
18	
19	    Input:
20	        x: (batch, n) fp32

2	display_name: "TopK via Bitonic Sort"

6	# Top-k is dominated by the input read (small output, no reduction over k).

8	# track them but score on bandwidth.
9	flops_formula: "batch * n * 4"            # ~O(n log^2 n) compares total, but the

1	"""SOTA reference for TopK: torch.topk itself.
2	
3	torch.topk dispatches to a CUB-backed kernel that uses radix-select for
4	moderate k and a tuned bitonic sort for small n. It is the bar the agent's
5	hand-rolled bitonic kernel must beat. There is no obvious vendor library that
6	does better on the (batch, n, k) shape mix we evaluate — Faiss BlockSelect is
7	specialized for k>=32 with much larger n, and CUB's DeviceSegmentedRadixSort
8	sorts the full row (overkill for top-k).
9	
10	This file is INTENTIONALLY allowed to call torch.topk because it is the SOTA
11	oracle, not the agent's submission. The agent's solution.py is forbidden from
12	using torch.topk (see problem.yaml.forbidden).
13	"""

reasoning (52264 chars)
We have PyTorch 2.11.0+cu130 and compute capability 12.0. Need to write a top-k kernel. Let me think about the approach. This is a memory-bound problem. For shape (1, 131072, 64), we need to read 131072*4 = 512KB per batch. With batch=1, this is just one row. We need to saturate DRAM bandwidth. Strategy: - Use a warp/CTA per row for batched cases - For the large single-row case (batch=1, n=131072), need to distribute work across many SMs. A good approach is probably a two-stage selection: 1. Each block processes a chunk of the row and produces a local top-k (e.g., top-128 using shared memory bitonic sort / selection). 2. Merge local results. Since k is small (<=64), and we need top-k, a good strategy: - For each row, tile the input across blocks. Each block selects top-K from its tile using shared memory/registers. - Then merge the per-block partial results. For small k, a simple sorted-array merge per thread block works well. Actually, for these shapes: - batch=1, n=131072, k=64: single row, very large. Need multi-block. - batch=64, n=8192, k=8: 64 rows, each row 8192 elements. Could do one block per row. - batch=32, n=16384, k=32: 32 rows, each 16384. One block per row. - batch=16, n=12000, k=16: 16 rows. One block per row. - batch=128, n=4096, k=1: argmax. One block per row or maybe multiple rows per block. Given Blackwell SM120 with 192 KB shared memory and high bandwidth, let's design: Approach: use Triton. Triton top-k implementations: - Each block handles one row. - Load row in tiles. - Maintain top-k buffer in shared memory as sorted descending array. - For each tile, merge tile into top-k using bitonic/local sort. For multi-block case (batch=1, n=131072), we can either: - Use persistent blocks across the row? But Triton doesn't support cross-block communication easily without atomic or second kernel. - Use one block per row but with enough threads to span the row. For n=131072, one block with 1024 threads would need ~128 iterations. With high memory bandwidth, each iteration reads 4KB per block. But we'd be limited by a single block's memory throughput. Better to use multiple blocks and merge. So two-kernel approach: 1. Kernel 1: each block handles a chunk of a row, produces local top-K. 2. Kernel 2: merge local top-K results. We can write this in Triton. But Triton on Blackwell might have limitations. Let me consider CUDA C++ via torch.utils.cpp_extension.load_inline instead for more control and ability to use features like warp shuffle, shared memory, etc. CUDA C++ approach: - Kernel 1: Each block reads a tile of elements. Maintain top-k in shared memory. Use bitonic sort or selection sort. Each block outputs top-(2*k) or top-k values and indices. - Kernel 2: merge per-block results. Actually, simpler: use a single warp-selection per row. But for large n and k=64, that's slow. Alternative: use CUB or thrust? But we need top-k not full sort. We can implement our own. Let me think about the most efficient known pattern for top-k on GPU: - For moderate k, a two-stage "radix select" or "bitonic top-k" is common. - A simple and effective approach for small k is "register file tournament" / "bitonic partial sort". For batch=1, n=131072, k=64, we could use one block with 1024 threads. Each thread maintains 64/32 = 2 candidates. That gives 2048 candidates, then reduce/merge to top-64. But that requires multiple passes over the data. Better: load chunks of 64 elements per thread (or per warp), keep top-k in registers, merge. For high performance, I think a 2-level reduction is best: - Level 1: Many blocks per row. Each block processes a contiguous chunk of input (e.g., 4096 elements) and uses shared memory to find top-(2*k) values/indices. Since chunk size >> k, we can use a full sort of chunk? No, chunk 4096 > k=64. Use selection: maintain a sorted top-(2*k) list, merge chunks of the chunk. - Level 2: One block per row reads all per-block top-(2*k) and merges to final top-k. Let me design in CUDA C++. Kernel details for per-block top-k: - Each block handles one "segment" of one row. - BlockDim = 256 threads. - Load input in tiles of BLOCK_THREADS * ITEMS_PER_THREAD = 256 * 8 = 2048 elements per tile (shared memory: 2048 * 4 = 8KB). - For each tile: find the local top-k within tile (using warp reductions and bitonic sort in shared memory), then merge with global top-k. Actually, simpler: each block processes one row and uses shared memory sort if n is small. For n=131072, one block is too slow. So we need multiple blocks per row. A clean approach: - Kernel 1: one block per (row, chunk). Each block produces top-K candidates from its chunk. Number of blocks = batch * ceil(n / CHUNK_SIZE). - Kernel 2: one block per row, merge all per-block top-K candidates into final top-k. CHUNK_SIZE should be chosen such that each block has enough work. For n=131072, with CHUNK_SIZE=4096, we'd have 32 blocks per row. For n=8192, 2 blocks per row. For n=4096, 1 block per row. But with batch=64 and n=8192, we'd have 128 blocks total, which is fine. For n=4096 with batch=128, we'd have 128 blocks. Wait, kernel 2 merges per-block top-K. For n=4096 k=1, kernel 1 produces 1 candidate per block, kernel 2 trivial. But for n=8192 with CHUNK_SIZE=4096, kernel 1 produces 2 candidates per row, kernel 2 merges 2 to 1. For n=12000, ceil(12000/4096)=3 blocks per row. So in kernel 1, each block needs to find top-K from its chunk of size CHUNK_SIZE. K is the problem's k. We can make it top-(2*K) for safety, but top-K is enough. How to find top-K from a chunk of CHUNK_SIZE elements: - Use shared memory to store the chunk (or tiles of it). - Maintain top-K values and indices in shared memory sorted descending. - For each tile, merge tile elements into top-K list. A simpler approach: fully sort the chunk using bitonic sort in shared memory. But CHUNK_SIZE=4096 with 8-byte key+value pairs = 32KB, fits. Sorting 4096 elements per block takes O(CHUNK_SIZE log² CHUNK_SIZE) comparisons, but all in fast shared memory. For k up to 64, sorting 4096 is overkill but might still be fast. Let me design Kernel 1 with tile-based merge: ```cpp template<int K, int TILE_SIZE, int BLOCK_THREADS> __global__ void topk_chunk_kernel(const float* __restrict__ input, int batch, int n, int k, float* __restrict__ out_values, int64_t* __restrict__ out_indices) { int row = blockIdx.x; int chunk = blockIdx.y; int tid = threadIdx.x; int chunk_start = chunk * CHUNK_SIZE; int chunk_end = min(chunk_start + CHUNK_SIZE, n); __shared__ float topk_vals[K]; __shared__ int64_t topk_idx[K]; // initialize top-k with -inf for (int i = tid; i < K; i += BLOCK_THREADS) { topk_vals[i] = -FLT_MAX; topk_idx[i] = -1; } __syncthreads(); // process input in tiles of TILE_SIZE for (int tile_start = chunk_start; tile_start < chunk_end; tile_start += TILE_SIZE) { __shared__ float tile_vals[TILE_SIZE]; __shared__ int64_t tile_idx[TILE_SIZE]; // load tile int tile_len = min(TILE_SIZE, chunk_end - tile_start); for (int i = tid; i < tile_len; i += BLOCK_THREADS) { tile_vals[i] = input[row * n + tile_start + i]; tile_idx[i] = tile_start + i; } for (int i = tile_len + tid; i < TILE_SIZE; i += BLOCK_THREADS) { tile_vals[i] = -FLT_MAX; tile_idx[i] = -1; } __syncthreads(); // bitonic sort tile descending by value bitonic_sort_descending<TILE_SIZE>(tile_vals, tile_idx); // merge top-K of tile with global top-K // ... need to merge tile_vals[0:K] (sorted desc) with topk_vals[0:K] (sorted desc) // result should be top-K of merged 2K. // Can do merge in shared memory. __syncthreads(); } // write out top-K int blocks_per_row = gridDim.y; for (int i = tid; i < k; i += BLOCK_THREADS) { out_values[row * blocks_per_row * k + chunk * k + i] = topk_vals[i]; out_indices[row * blocks_per_row * k + chunk * k + i] = topk_idx[i]; } } ``` Need bitonic sort and merge functions. Implementation plan for solution.py: ```python import torch import torch.nn as nn from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline CUDA_SOURCE = r''' #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> #include <cfloat> #include <cstdint> template <int N> __device__ void bitonic_sort_descending(float* __restrict__ vals, int64_t* __restrict__ idx) { #pragma unroll for (int k = 2; k <= N; k <<= 1) { #pragma unroll for (int j = k >> 1; j > 0; j >>= 1) { int tid = threadIdx.x; for (int i = tid; i < N; i += blockDim.x) { if ((i & j) == 0) { int ixj = i ^ j; bool up = (i & k) != 0; float vi = vals[i]; float vj = vals[ixj]; int64_t ii = idx[i]; int64_t ij = idx[ixj]; bool swap = up ? (vi > vj) : (vi < vj); if (swap) { vals[i] = vj; vals[ixj] = vi; idx[i] = ij; idx[ixj] = ii; } } } __syncthreads(); } } } template <int CHUNK_SIZE> __global__ void topk_chunk_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, int batch, int n, int k, float* __restrict__ out_vals, int64_t* __restrict__ out_idx, int blocks_per_row ) { int row = blockIdx.x; int chunk = blockIdx.y; int tid = threadIdx.x; if (row >= batch) return; int chunk_start = chunk * CHUNK_SIZE; int chunk_end = min(chunk_start + CHUNK_SIZE, n); int row_offset = row * n + chunk_start; __shared__ float svals[CHUNK_SIZE]; __shared__ int64_t sidx[CHUNK_SIZE]; // load chunk with padding to CHUNK_SIZE for (int i = tid; i < CHUNK_SIZE; i += blockDim.x) { if (chunk_start + i < chunk_end) { svals[i] = input[row_offset + i]; sidx[i] = chunk_start + i; } else { svals[i] = -FLT_MAX; sidx[i] = -1; } } __syncthreads(); bitonic_sort_descending<CHUNK_SIZE>(svals, sidx); // write top-k int out_offset = row * blocks_per_row * k + chunk * k; for (int i = tid; i < k; i += blockDim.x) { out_vals[out_offset + i] = svals[i]; out_idx[out_offset + i] = sidx[i]; } } __global__ void topk_merge_kernel( const float* __restrict__ in_vals, const int64_t* __restrict__ in_idx, int batch, int blocks_per_row, int k, float* __restrict__ out_vals, int64_t* __restrict__ out_idx ) { int row = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; if (row >= batch) return; // Load all candidates into shared memory and pad to power of 2 int total = blocks_per_row * k; int N = 1; while (N < total) N <<= 1; extern __shared__ char smem[]; float* svals = (float*)smem; int64_t* sidx = (int64_t*)(smem + N * sizeof(float)); int in_offset = row * blocks_per_row * k; for (int i = tid; i < N; i += blockDim.x) { if (i < total) { svals[i] = in_vals[in_offset + i]; sidx[i] = in_idx[in_offset + i]; } else { svals[i] = -FLT_MAX; sidx[i] = -1; } } __syncthreads(); // Sort using a runtime-determined N. Since N depends on blocks_per_row and k, // we can't easily templatize. We can dispatch or use a loop-based bitonic sort. // For simplicity, use loop-based bitonic sort. for (int kk = 2; kk <= N; kk <<= 1) { for (int j = kk >> 1; j > 0; j >>= 1) { for (int i = tid; i < N; i += blockDim.x) { if ((i & j) == 0) { int ixj = i ^ j; bool up = (i & kk) != 0; float vi = svals[i], vj = svals[ixj]; int64_t ii = sidx[i], ij = sidx[ixj]; bool swap = up ? (vi > vj) : (vi < vj); if (swap) { svals[i] = vj; svals[ixj] = vi; sidx[i] = ij; sidx[ixj] = ii; } } } __syncthreads(); } } for (int i = tid; i < k; i += blockDim.x) { out_vals[row * k + i] = svals[i]; out_idx[row * k + i] = sidx[i]; } } ''' ``` Wait, the merge kernel needs runtime N, so I need a non-templated bitonic sort. +"""Custom CUDA top-k over the last dim.
+
+Two-level bitonic sort:
+  1. Each CUDA block sorts a 1024-element chunk of its row and writes the top-k
+     values/indices to an intermediate buffer.
+  2. A second kernel merges the per-chunk top-k lists and returns the final
+     sorted top-k.
+
+All sorting is descending by value. Padding uses a very negative sentinel so
+it sinks to the bottom of the network.
+"""
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline
+
+
+CUDA_SOURCE = r'''
+#include <torch/extension.h>
+#include <cuda_runtime.h>
+#include <cfloat>
+#include <cstdint>
+#include <vector>
+
+// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
+// Bitonic sort, descending by value.  N must be a power of two and is known at
+// compile time.  Comparators are assigned to threads so that each pair is
+// touched exactly once per (k,j) sub-stage.
+// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
+template <int N>
+__device__ __forceinline__ void bitonic_sort_descending(float* __restrict__ vals,
+                                                         int64_t* __restrict__ idx) {
+    #pragma unroll
+    for (int kk = 2; kk <= N; kk <<= 1) {
+        #pragma unroll
+        for (int j = kk >> 1; j > 0; j >>= 1) {
+            for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < N; i += blockDim.x) {
+                if ((i & j) == 0) {
+                    int ixj = i ^ j;
+                    bool up = (i & kk) != 0;          // true -> want smaller value at i
+                    float vi = vals[i];
+                    float vj = vals[ixj];
+                    bool swap = up ? (vi > vj) : (vi < vj);
+                    if (swap) {
+                        vals[i] = vj;
+                        vals[ixj] = vi;
+                        int64_t ii = idx[i];
+                        int64_t ij = idx[ixj];
+                        idx[i] = ij;
+                        idx[ixj] = ii;
+                    }
+                }
+            }
+            __syncthreads();
+        }
+    }
+}
+
+// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
+// Runtime-sized bitonic sort for the merge stage.  N is a power of two and is
+// bounded by the merge buffer size (MAX_MERGE_N).
+// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
+__device__ __forceinline__ void bitonic_sort_descending_runtime(float* __restrict__ vals,
+                                                                 int64_t* __restrict__ idx,
+                                                                 int N) {
+    for (int kk = 2; kk <= N; kk <<= 1) {
+        for (int j = kk >> 1; j > 0; j >>= 1) {
+            for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < N; i += blockDim.x) {
+                if ((i & j) == 0) {
+                    int ixj = i ^ j;
+                    bool up = (i & kk) != 0;
+                    float vi = vals[i];
+                    float vj = vals[ixj];
+                    bool swap = up ? (vi > vj) : (vi < vj);
+                    if (swap) {
+                        vals[i] = vj;
+                        vals[ixj] = vi;
+                        int64_t ii = idx[i];
+                        int64_t ij = idx[ixj];
+                        idx[i] = ij;
+                        idx[ixj] = ii;
+                    }
+                }
+            }
+            __syncthreads();
+        }
+    }
+}
+
+// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
+// Level 1: sort a chunk and write its top-k.
+// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
+template <int CHUNK_SIZE>
+__global__ void topk_chunk_kernel(const float* __restrict__ input,
+                                  int batch, int n, int k,
+                                  float* __restrict__ out_vals,
+                                  int64_t* __restrict__ out_idx,
+                                  int blocks_per_row) {
+    int row = blockIdx.x;
+    int chunk = blockIdx.y;
+    int tid = threadIdx.x;
+    if (row >= batch) return;
+
+    int chunk_start = chunk * CHUNK_SIZE;
+    int chunk_end = min(chunk_start + CHUNK_SIZE, n);
+    const float* row_ptr = input + row * n;
+
+    __shared__ float svals[CHUNK_SIZE];
+    __shared__ int64_t sidx[CHUNK_SIZE];
+
+    // Load chunk and pad to CHUNK_SIZE with a sentinel that sinks to the end.
+    for (int i = tid; i < CHUNK_SIZE; i += blockDim.x) {
+        if (chunk_start + i < chunk_end) {
+            svals[i] = row_ptr[chunk_start + i];
+            sidx[i] = chunk_start + i;
+        } else {
+            svals[i] = -FLT_MAX;
+            sidx[i] = 0;
+        }
+    }
+    __syncthreads();
+
+    bitonic_sort_descending<CHUNK_SIZE>(svals, sidx);
+
+    int out_offset = row * blocks_per_row * k + chunk * k;
+    for (int i = tid; i < k; i += blockDim.x) {
+        out_vals[out_offset + i] = svals[i];
+        out_idx[out_offset + i] = sidx[i];
+    }
+}
+
+// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
+// Level 2: merge per-chunk top-k lists into the final top-k.
+// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
+#define MAX_MERGE_N 8192
+
+__global__ void topk_merge_kernel(const float* __restrict__ in_vals,
+                                  const int64_t* __restrict__ in_idx,
+                                  int batch, int blocks_per_row, int k,
+                                  float* __restrict__ out_vals,
+                                  int64_t* __restrict__ out_idx) {
+    int row = blockIdx.x;
+    int tid = threadIdx.x;
+    if (row >= batch) return;
+
+    int total = blocks_per_row * k;
+    int N = 1;

1	"""Custom CUDA top-k over the last dim.
2	
3	Two-level bitonic sort:
4	  1. Each CUDA block sorts a 1024-element chunk of its row and writes the top-k
5	     values/indices to an intermediate buffer.
6	  2. A second kernel merges the per-chunk top-k lists and returns the final
7	     sorted top-k.
8	
9	All sorting is descending by value. Padding uses a very negative sentinel so
10	it sinks to the bottom of the network.
11	"""
12	import torch
13	import torch.nn as nn
14	from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline
15

17	CUDA_SOURCE = r'''
18	#include <torch/extension.h>
19	#include <cuda_runtime.h>
20	#include <cfloat>
21	#include <cstdint>
22	#include <vector>
23	
24	// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
25	// Bitonic sort, descending by value.  N must be a power of two and is known at
26	// compile time.  Comparators are assigned to threads so that each pair is
27	// touched exactly once per (k,j) sub-stage.
28	// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
29	template <int N>
30	__device__ __forceinline__ void bitonic_sort_descending(float* __restrict__ vals,
31	                                                         int64_t* __restrict__ idx) {
32	    #pragma unroll
33	    for (int kk = 2; kk <= N; kk <<= 1) {
34	        #pragma unroll
35	        for (int j = kk >> 1; j > 0; j >>= 1) {
36	            for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < N; i += blockDim.x) {
37	                if ((i & j) ==

device = torch.device('cuda:0')
shape = shapes.SHAPES[0]
reference.batch = shape['batch']
reference.n = shape['n']
reference.k = shape['k']
model = solution.Model(*reference.get_init_inputs()).to(device).eval()
torch.manual_seed(2026)
inputs = [t.to(device) for t in reference.get_inputs()]
with torch.no_grad():
    out = model(*inputs)

torch.cuda.synchronize()

import torch
import time
import shapes

device = torch.device('cuda:0')
for sidx, shape in enumerate(shapes.SHAPES):
    batch, n, k = shape['batch'], shape['n'], shape['k']
    x = torch.randn(batch, n, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
    # warmup
    for _ in range(10):
        v, i = torch.topk(x, k, dim=-1, largest=True, sorted=True)
    torch.cuda.synchronize()
    t0 = time.perf_counter()
    for _ in range(100):
        v, i = torch.topk(x, k, dim=-1, largest=True, sorted=True)
    torch.cuda.synchronize()
    t1 = time.perf_counter()
    ms = (t1 - t0) / 100 * 1000
    bytes_moved = batch * n * 4 + batch * k * (4 + 8)
    gbps = bytes_moved / (ms / 1000) / 1e9
    print(f'shape={sidx} n={n} k={k} ms={ms:.4f} gbps={gbps:.1f}')
"

43	    """Evict L2 by writing 128 MB on the GPU."""

This avoids the two-kernel overhead and should be faster. For shape 0 (n=131072), one block processing the whole row. With 256 threads, each thread processes 512 elements. Total tiles = 131072 / 256 = 512 tiles. For each tile (256 elements), sort in shared memory, take top-K, merge with block top-K. But one block for n=131072 is underutilized. With 256 threads, memory parallelism is limited. But it avoids multi-block merge. Let me estimate time: 512 tiles * sort 256 (~16k comparators) = 8.2M comparators. With 256 threads, 32k comparator ops per thread. At 1 GHz, 32 us. Memory read 512KB at maybe 100 GB/s (limited by one block) = 5 us. Total ~37 us = 0.037 ms. That's close to torch.topk's 0.049 ms. Good! For shape 1 (64 rows, n=8192), one block per row => 64 blocks. Each block processes 8192/256=32 tiles. Per block: 32*16k = 512k comparators. 64 blocks = 32M comparators. For shape 4 (128 rows, n=4096, k=1), one block per row => 128 blocks. Each block processes 16 tiles of 256. Sort 256 each. That's wasteful for k=1. We can special-case k=1 with argmax. But let's first implement the general tile-based single-kernel and see. Actually, for k=1, we can use a simple block-level reduction (argmax). That's very fast. For general k, tile-based selection. Let me design the single-kernel tile-based top-k: ```cpp template <int TILE_SIZE, int BLOCK_THREADS> __global__ void topk_row_kernel(const float* input, int batch, int n, int k, float* out_vals, int64_t* out_idx) { int row = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; if (row >= batch) return; const float* row_ptr = input + row * n; __shared__ float topk_vals[K_MAX]; // we need K max, but K is runtime. Use dynamic? __shared__ int64_t topk_idx[K_MAX]; // initialize top-k for (int i = tid; i < k; i += BLOCK_THREADS) { topk_vals[i] = -FLT_MAX; topk_idx[i] = 0; } __syncthreads(); __shared__ float tile_vals[TILE_SIZE]; __shared__ int64_t tile_idx[TILE_SIZE]; for (int tile_start = 0; tile_start < n; tile_start += TILE_SIZE) { int tile_len = min(TILE_SIZE, n - tile_start); // load tile for (int i = tid; i < TILE_SIZE; i += BLOCK_THREADS) { if (i < tile_len) { tile_vals[i] = row_ptr[tile_start + i]; tile_idx[i] = tile_start + i; } else { tile_vals[i] = -FLT_MAX; tile_idx[i] = 0; } } __syncthreads(); // sort tile descending bitonic_sort_descending<TILE_SIZE>(tile_vals, tile_idx); // merge tile top-k into block top-k // Both are sorted descending. Merge first k of tile with block top-k. // Need cooperative merge. __syncthreads(); } // write top-k for (int i = tid; i < k; i += BLOCK_THREADS) { out_vals[row * k + i] = topk_vals[i]; out_idx[row * k + i] = top_idx[i]; } } ``` The merge is tricky. Both block top-k and tile top-k are sorted descending. We need to merge them and keep top-k. Since both arrays are sorted, we can do a standard merge. But with K elements each, merging produces 2K sorted, then take first K. This can be done cooperatively in shared memory. Simpler: after sorting tile, the tile's top-k are at tile_vals[0:k]. We can copy them to a temporary array along with block top-k, sort the combined array (size 2k), and take top-k. But 2k sort for each tile. For k=64, 2k=128. Sorting 128 each tile. The standard approach is to maintain block top-K and merge each tile's top-K into it. The merge cost is O(K) per tile using a standard merge of two sorted arrays. We can do this cooperatively. How to merge two sorted arrays of size K into top-K efficiently in CUDA: - Use all threads. Each thread takes one position i in output (0..K-1). - Output[i] is the i-th largest of the merged 2K array. - To find output[i], we can use binary search: for each element in A, find its rank in B. - But that's O(K log K) with K threads. Hmm. torch.topk is 5x faster than memory-bound full sort. So it really uses a clever selection. We need to implement something like radix select or bitonic select. Let me look at how to implement radix top-k. **Radix select for top-k:** 1. For each bit from MSB to LSB, count how many elements have that bit set (among candidates). 2. If count >= k, keep only elements with bit set; else keep all, decrement k by count, move to next bit. 3. After all bits, we have the k-th largest value threshold. 4. Gather all elements >= threshold, sort top-k. This is O(N * bits) for counting + O(N) for gather + O(k log k) for sort. For N=131072, bits=32, total ~4M operations. Much less than full sort. But implementing in CUDA with multiple blocks and global atomics is complex. Simpler: use a single block per row and do radix select in shared memory. But for n=131072, one block can't hold all elements. We can do multi-block radix select: - Each block processes a chunk and maintains counts per bit bucket in shared memory, then atomicAdd to global counts. - Need multiple passes (one per bit) with global synchronization. Hard without multiple kernels. Alternative: bitonic selection network. For top-k, there's a bitonic selection network that produces the top-k unsorted or sorted with fewer comparators than full sort. A bitonic top-k network has O(N log² K) comparators. For N=1024, K=64, that's 1024 * 36 = 37k comparators vs full sort 100k. Modest improvement. Radix select algorithm for top-k: - Convert floats to uint32 keys (xor sign bit to get descending order). - For each bit from MSB (bit 31) down to bit 0: - Count number of candidate keys with bit = 1. - If count >= k: keep only candidates with bit = 1. - Else: keep all candidates, k -= count. - After all bits, the kept candidates are the top-k.  """Custom CUDA top-k over the last dim.
 
-Strategy:
-  * k == 1: dedicated warp-reduction argmax.
-  * k > 1: CUB DeviceSegmentedRadixSort per row (descending by value, value
-    payload = original index), then copy the first k entries of each sorted
-    segment to the output.  CUB's device sort is highly optimized and uses
-    all SMs, which is especially important for the single-row large-vocab
-    decoder shape.
+Two-level radix sort via CUB:
+  1. Each CUDA block fully sorts a 512-element chunk with CUB BlockRadixSort
+     (key = value, value = local index as int32) and writes the top-k.
+  2. A second kernel merges the per-chunk top-k lists into the final sorted
+     top-k.  Internal indices are int32 to fit larger merges in shared memory;
+     the final output is cast to int64.
+
+k == 1 uses a dedicated argmax reduction path.

 constexpr int BLOCK_THREADS = 256;
-constexpr int CHUNK_SIZE = 4096;
+constexpr int CHUNK_SIZE = 512;
+constexpr int ITEMS_PER_THREAD = CHUNK_SIZE / BLOCK_THREADS;   // 2
 constexpr int K_MAX = 64;
 
 // -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
-// k == 1: argmax per chunk, then merge per row.
+// Bitonic sort for small runtime-sized arrays of float+int32.
+// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
+__device__ __forceinline__ void bitonic_sort_descending_runtime(float* __restrict__ vals,
+                                                                 int32_t* __restrict__ idx,
+                                                                 int N) {
+    for (int kk = 2; kk <= N; kk <<= 1) {
+        for (int j = kk >> 1; j > 0; j >>= 1) {
+            for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < N; i += blockDim.x) {
+                if ((i & j) == 0) {
+                    int ixj = i ^ j;
+                    bool up = (i & kk) != 0;
+                    float vi = vals[i];
+                    float vj = vals[ixj];
+                    bool swap = up ? (vi > vj) : (vi < vj);
+                    if (swap) {
+                        vals[i] = vj;
+                        vals[ixj] = vi;
+                        int32_t ii = idx[i];
+                        int32_t ij = idx[ixj];
+                        idx[i] = ij;
+                        idx[ixj] = ii;
+                    }
+                }
+            }
+            __syncthreads();
+        }
+    }
+}
+
+// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
+// Level 1: CUB radix-sort a chunk and write its top-k (values + int32 idx).
+// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
+__global__ void topk_chunk_kernel(const float* __restrict__ input,
+                                  int batch, int n, int k,
+                                  float* __restrict__ out_vals,
+                                  int32_t* __restrict__ out_idx,
+                                  int blocks_per_row) {
+    using BlockRadixSort = cub::BlockRadixSort<float, BLOCK_THREADS, ITEMS_PER_THREAD, int32_t>;
+    __shared__ typename BlockRadixSort::TempStorage temp_storage;
+
+    int row = blockIdx.x;
+    int chunk = blockIdx.y;
+    int tid = threadIdx.x;
+    if (row >= batch) return;
+
+    int chunk_start = chunk * CHUNK_SIZE;
+    int chunk_end = min(chunk_start + CHUNK_SIZE, n);
+    const float* row_ptr = input + row * n;
+
+    float thread_keys[ITEMS_PER_THREAD];
+    int32_t thread_values[ITEMS_PER_THREAD];
+
+    #pragma unroll
+    for (int i = 0; i < ITEMS_PER_THREAD; ++i) {
+        int pos = chunk_start + tid + i * BLOCK_THREADS;
+        if (pos < chunk_end) {
+            thread_keys[i] = row_ptr[pos];
+            thread_values[i] = pos;
+        } else {
+            thread_keys[i] = -FLT_MAX;
+            thread_values[i] = 0;
+        }
+    }
+
+    BlockRadixSort(temp_storage).SortDescendingBlockedToStriped(thread_keys, thread_values);
+
+    if (tid < k) {
+        int out_offset = row * blocks_per_row * k + chunk * k;
+        out_vals[out_offset + tid] = thread_keys[0];
+        out_idx[out_offset + tid] = thread_values[0];
+    }
+}
+

+// Dedicated k == 1 argmax per chunk.
 // -----------------------------------------------------------------------------

                                     int batch, int n,

 """Custom CUDA top-k over the last dim.
 
-Two-level radix sort via CUB:
-  1. Each CUDA block fully sorts a 512-element chunk with CUB BlockRadixSort
-     (key = value, value = local index as int32) and writes the top-k.
-  2. A second kernel merges the per-chunk top-k lists into the final sorted
-     top-k.  Internal indices are int32 to fit larger merges in shared memory;
-     the final output is cast to int64.
-
-k == 1 uses a dedicated argmax reduction path.
+Hybrid strategy:
+  * k == 1: dedicated warp-reduction argmax.
+  * batch == 1: single CUB DeviceRadixSort over the row, then copy top-k.
+    This gives the large single-row decoder-vocab shape full SM utilization.
+  * batch > 1: CUB BlockRadixSort per 1024-element chunk, then merge per-chunk
+    top-k lists in shared memory.
 """

+// k == 1: argmax per chunk, then merge per row.
+// -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
+__global__ void argmax_chunk_kernel(const float* __restrict__ input,
+                                    int batch, int n,
+                                    float* __restrict__ out_vals,
+                                    int64_t* __restrict__ out_idx,
+                                    int blocks_per_row) {
     int row = blockIdx.x;
     int chunk = blockIdx.y;
     int tid = threadIdx.x;
     if (row >= batch) return;
 
+    int chunk_start = chunk * 4096;
+    int chunk_end = min(chunk_start + 4096, n);
+    const float* row_ptr = input + row * n;
+
+    float local_max = -FLT_MAX;
+    int64_t local_idx = 0;
+    for (int i = chunk_start + tid; i < chunk_end; i += blockDim.x) {
+        float v = row_ptr[i];
+        if (v > local_max) {
+            local_max = v;
+            local_idx = i;
+        }
+    }
+
+    #pragma unroll
+    for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) {
+        float other_val = __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, local_max, offset);
+        int64_t other_idx = __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, local_idx, offset);
+        if (other_val > local_max) {
+            local_max = other_val;
+            local_idx = other_idx;
+        }
+    }
+
+    __shared__ float warp_max[BLOCK_THREADS / 32];
+    __shared__ int64_t warp_idx[BLOCK_THREADS / 32];
+    int lane = tid & 31;
+    int warp_id = tid >> 5;
+    if (lane == 0) {
+        warp_max[warp_id] = local_max;
+        warp_idx[warp_id] = local_idx;
+    }
+    __syncthreads();
+
+    if (tid < (BLOCK_THREADS / 32)) {
+        local_max = warp_max[tid];
+        local_idx = warp_idx[tid];
+    } else {
+        local_max = -FLT_MAX;
+        local_idx = 0;
+    }
+    __syncthreads();
+
+    #pragma unroll
+    for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) {
+        float other_val = __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, local_max, offset);
+        int64_t other_idx = __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, local_idx, offset);
+        if (other_val > local_max) {
+            local_max = other_val;
+            local_idx = other_idx;
+        }
+    }
+
+    if (tid == 0) {
+        int out_offset = row * blocks_per_row + chunk;
+        out_vals[out_offset] = local_max;
+        out_idx[out_offset] = local_idx;
+    }
+}

+void topk_argmax_forward(torch::Tensor input, int64_t k,
+                         torch::Tensor values, torch::Tensor indices,
+                         torch::Tensor tmp_vals, torch::Tensor tmp_idx) {
+    int batch = input.size(0);
+    int n = input.size(1);
+    int blocks_per_row = (n + ARGMAX_CHUNK - 1) / ARGMAX_CHUNK;
+
+    if (blocks_per_row == 1) {
+        dim3 grid(batch, 1);
+        argmax_chunk_kernel<<<grid, BLOCK_THREADS>>>(
+            input.data_ptr<float>(), batch, n,
+            values.data_ptr<float>(), indices.data_ptr<int64_t>(), 1);
+    } else {
+        dim3 grid1(batch, blocks_per_row);
+        argmax_chunk_kernel<<<grid1, BLOCK_THREADS>>>(
+            input.data_ptr<float>(), batch, n,
+            tmp_vals.data_ptr<float>(), tmp_idx.data_ptr<int64_t>(), blocks_per_row);
+

+            tmp_vals.data_ptr<float>(), tmp_idx.data_ptr<int64_t>(),
+            batch, blocks_per_row,
+            values.data_ptr<float>(), indices.data_ptr<int64_t>());
+    }
